## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / nonlinear oscillators
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the equation of motion (acceleration) for a nonlinear harmonic oscillator. The acceleration dv_dt is likely a function of position x and velocity v, representing restoring forces (potentially nonlinear in x) and damping forces (potentially nonlinear in v). Time t may appear explicitly if the system is driven or non-autonomous.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (harmonic external forcing)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (quadratic nonlinearity in restoring force)
- General polynomial restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (polynomial potential)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-dependent nonlinear damping)
- Coulomb + viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * Abs(v) (quadratic drag + restoring)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (time-varying stiffness)
- Damped Duffing with quadratic: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (general polynomial restoring + damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) → symmetric potential wells preserving oscillation symmetry
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v → linear energy dissipation or injection (linear damping/anti-damping)
- Position-velocity coupling like x**2 * v → amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of Van der Pol-type oscillators
- Even-power position terms (x**2) → asymmetric potential leading to asymmetric oscillations and DC offset
- Sinusoidal time dependence sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) → external periodic driving force causing resonance phenomena
- Cubic position term x**3 with opposite sign to linear term → Duffing-type hardening or softening spring behavior
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous system where phase portrait fully characterizes dynamics
- Products of velocity powers with position powers (v * x**n) → nonlinear dissipation mechanisms tied to displacement

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.0892421*v³ - 0.725306*v*(1 - x²) - 1.44736*x - 1.44736*x*exp(-|x|)`

Expanding: `-0.0892421*v³ - 0.725306*v + 0.725306*v*x² - 1.44736*x - 1.44736*x*exp(-|x|)`

So the GT has these basis functions:
- `v³` (coefficient ≈ -0.0892)
- `v` (coefficient ≈ -0.7253)
- `v*x²` (coefficient ≈ 0.7253)
- `x` (coefficient ≈ -1.4474)
- `x*exp(-|x|)` (coefficient ≈ -1.4474)

The key non-standard term is `x*exp(-|x|)`. This is NOT a polynomial, NOT a simple trigonometric function, and NOT expressible as standard elementary functions without absolute value in the exponent.

Let me check which candidates can reproduce `x*exp(-|x|)`:

**Key question:** Can any candidate's basis functions exactly reproduce `x*exp(-|x|)`?

`x*exp(-|x|)` is an even-like function in some sense but specifically: for x>0 it's `x*exp(-x)` and for x<0 it's `x*exp(x)`. This function is smooth, non-polynomial, and cannot be expressed as a finite combination of polynomials, `sin`, `cos`, `log`, or simple exponentials.

Let me go through candidates systematically:

**Candidates with only polynomial + v terms (no transcendental x-terms):** 3, 5, 6, 45, 47, etc. — These CANNOT match because polynomials can't equal `x*exp(-|x|)`. **NO MATCH** for all purely polynomial candidates.

**Candidates with `sin(c*x)` terms:** 1, 13, 22, 24, 27, 35, 40, 41, 58, etc. — `sin(cx)` cannot reproduce `x*exp(-|x|)`. **NO MATCH**.

**Candidates with `log(c*x²+1)` terms:** 13, 18, 46 — `x*log(cx²+1)` or `log(cx²+1)` cannot equal `x*exp(-|x|)`. **NO MATCH**.

**Candidates with `x*exp(c*x²)` terms:** 15, 49, 52 — `x*exp(cx²)` is symmetric in x (even times odd = odd), but `exp(cx²)` ≠ `exp(-|x|)`. **NO MATCH**.

**Candidates with `exp(c*x)` terms:** 49 has `x*exp(c9*x)` — this only works for one sign of x. **NO MATCH**.

**Candidates with `x/(c+v)^n` or similar v-dependent rational terms:** These introduce v-dependence that doesn't match. **NO MATCH**.

**Candidate 73:** `c0*x + c1*sin(c2*x) + c3*v + c4*v*x² + c5*v³ + c6*log(c7*exp(c8*x) + 1)`

The term `log(c7*exp(c8*x) + 1)` is a softplus-like function. For the GT we need `x*exp(-|x|)`. This is NOT equivalent. **NO MATCH**.

**Candidates with rational forms (fractions):** 2, 4, 7, 8, 9, 10, 11, 12, 16 — These simplify to polynomial + `c0*x/(c1*x²+1)` type terms. The term `x/(c*x²+1)` resembles a Lorentzian-like function, NOT `x*exp(-|x|)`. **NO MATCH**.

**Candidates with `v**5` terms:** 17, 31, 32, 33, 37, 38, 39, 43, 62, 64, 67, 70 — Even if we set v⁵ coefficient to 0, the remaining terms can't produce `x*exp(-|x|)`. **NO MATCH**.

After checking ALL 73 candidates, none contain a basis function that can exactly reproduce `x*exp(-|x|)`. The GT's distinctive term `x*exp(-|x|)` (which involves an absolute value in the exponent) is not representable by any combination of the basis functions available in any candidate.
